My first job in data was as an analyst, and it was my responsibility to work with system owners to source data, help raise and fix data quality issues, etc..

I&#39;m now at a much larger company, and our analyst partners don&#39;t really seem to be capable of digging into the data. They usually just use the highly-curated tables maintained by engineering, but if they do dig into source data, they rarely if ever communicate with the product / IT / ops teams that maintain the fields. I think the engineers should be able to point the analyst in the right direction, maybe give some pointers. But the analyst probably shouldn&#39;t take that at face value either and verify if there&#39;s any uncertainty on what fields mean.</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--multiline nohighlight">with open(&#39;uploadable.txt&#39;, &#39;w&#39;) as f:

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1304661137144680480 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1304661137144680480><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/854815798925328454/761043d6e6e674ea267f4f774ea9759c.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=rcdpge data-user-id=854815798925328454>Robert</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Saturday, November 9, 2024 1:17 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1304661137144680480>11/9/2024 1:17 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>What is the difference between a standard API and a RESTful API</span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Saturday, November 9, 2024 1:17 AM">(edited)</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1304671716722741318 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1304671716722741318><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/256442550683041793/957261bc8f0ac51195cdaa3270bfc93a.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/854815798925328454/761043d6e6e674ea267f4f774ea9759c.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title=rcdpge>Robert</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'1304661137144680480')"> What is the difference between a standard API and a RESTful API </span> <span class=chatlog__reply-edited-timestamp title="Saturday, November 9, 2024 1:17 AM">(edited)</span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=etrotta data-user-id=256442550683041793>etrotta</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Saturday, November 9, 2024 1:59 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1304671716722741318>11/9/2024 1:59 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve><a href="&lt;https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/API&gt;">API</a> is an extremely generic term that covers nearly anything you can interact with via a programming interface, for example the standard library and third-party packages for programming languages can also be referred to as APIs in some contexts, or even some Operating System functions in some scenarios
(e.g. &quot;the numpy API&quot; or &quot;the file system API&#39;)

<a href="&lt;https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/REST&gt;">REST</a>ful APIs refer to a subset of APIs that follow a set of rules, in particular <em>stateless</em> web APIs

A fairly huge % of web APIs are RESTful APIs, and a lot of the time when someone is referring to something as an API they just mean a web RESTful API - specially if it&#39;s something like <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">&lt;... service&gt; API</code> like Google search</span></div><div class=chatlog__reactions><div class=chatlog__reaction title=SquirtleSquadCool><img class="chatlog__emoji chatlog__emoji--small" alt=SquirtleSquadCool src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/emojis/894685264935518220.png loading=lazy> <span class=chatlog__reaction-count>2</span></div></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1304757603049537597 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1304757603049537597><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/389497659087650836/788d735311609a0e8994463fe720dfdf.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author style=color:rgb(52,152,219) title=salt_rock_lamp data-user-id=389497659087650836>salt rock lamp</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Saturday, November 9, 2024 7:40 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1304757603049537597>11/9/2024 7:40 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>REST is weird because the original definition and the creator&#39;s original vision is not what most people have in mind when they use the term</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1304758161466724384 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1304758161466724384><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Saturday, November 9, 2024 7:43 AM">7:43 AM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Hence &quot;RESTful&quot; which is meant to imply &quot;kind of like REST but not entirely&quot;.

Usually it means using HTTP verbs aligned with API semantics (eg POST or PUT to create a new instance of something), URLs that are aligned with &quot;resources&quot; (<code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">/users/1234/bookmarks</code>), requests that are &quot;stateless&quot; in that each request contains all necessary information to carry out the request, and request and response bodies in JSON format</span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Saturday, November 9, 2024 7:46 AM">(edited)</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1304759275754754059 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1304759275754754059><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Saturday, November 9, 2024 7:47 AM">7:47 AM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve><a href="https://ics.uci.edu/~fielding/pubs/dissertation/rest_arch_style.htm">https://ics.uci.edu/~fielding/pubs/dissertation/rest_arch_style.htm</a></span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Saturday, November 9, 2024 7:47 AM">(edited)</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1304759962836144180 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1304759962836144180><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Saturday, November 9, 2024 7:50 AM">7:50 AM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve><div class="chatlog__markdown-quote"><div class="chatlog__markdown-quote-border"></div><div class="chatlog__markdown-quote-content">The REST interface is designed to be efficient for large-grain hypermedia data transfer, optimizing for the common case of the Web, but resulting in an interface that is not optimal for other forms of architectural interaction.</div></div></span></div></div></div></div></div>

We do use s3 in lakehouses in the sense that our entire lake is mounted to Databricks as external tables, and is materially just Deltas on s3.</span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Wednesday, November 13, 2024 5:40 AM">(edited)</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1306176461807419433 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1306176461807419433><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Wednesday, November 13, 2024 5:38 AM">5:38 AM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Mostly due to vendor lock-in/accessibility concerns, if some team wants that data but for some reason does not want to use Databricks, they can ingest from the s3, and benefit from understandable &quot;folder&quot; structure, which managed tables (AFAIK) do not provide. 
We also had a similar approach for other usecases like: Team A provides weekly reports for business users and does not use Databricks, Team B runs ML on Databricks and wants to mine these reports for features. So Team A uploads their reports on S3, the S3 is mounted as an external table, Team B&#39;s clusters can read it.</span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Wednesday, November 13, 2024 5:46 AM">(edited)</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<ul><li>you can only request so many access tokens per second, so if this is a web app generating hundreds or thousands of connections per second, you probably need to stick with username/PW auth</li><li>the request token endpoint will spit you out a token even if your role can’t actually connect, which is probably good from a security posture perspective, but don’t count on “being able to generate an auth token” being a good proxy for “being able to connect” </li><li>some AWS DBs IAM auth (Dynamo, Timestream, basically the serverless ones) also abstract network connectivity into IAM auth, Aurora doesn’t. This might be obvious to you, but it’s not in the docs. </li><li>lots of stuff like the PG TF provider don’t support IAM auth so we haven’t been able to switch over all service accounts. You also need some cert bundles installed on the machines you’re connecting with, but it seems like most have this by default if they have the AWS libraries present</li></ul></span></div><div class=chatlog__reactions><div class=chatlog__reaction title=thumbsup><img class="chatlog__emoji chatlog__emoji--small" alt=👍 src=https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/twitter/twemoji@latest/assets/svg/1f44d.svg loading=lazy> <span class=chatlog__reaction-count>1</span></div></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1306962657215250453 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1306962657215250453><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/3.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=philliphenry data-user-id=462278067474137088>PhillHenry</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Friday, November 15, 2024 9:42 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1306962657215250453>11/15/2024 9:42 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>I was told that the law of dashboards is:

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1306968033427980403 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1306968033427980403><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/105378403699408896/6ad9a21f4adaeee654f83a08a1327a68.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/3.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title=philliphenry>PhillHenry</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'1306962657215250453')"> I was told that the law of dashboards is: 
&quot;the number of people who find a dashboard useful is inversely proportional to its total information.&quot;

It seems dashboards die as more data is added to them in a misguided attempt to please more stakeholders. But those same people find the noise-to-signal ratio growing over time and ultimately stop using them in any meaningful way. YMMV. </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author style=color:rgb(231,76,60) title=emikachi data-user-id=105378403699408896>emily</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Friday, November 15, 2024 10:04 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1306968033427980403>11/15/2024 10:04 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>this has been my experience too

Dashboards should be legible and maximise signal:noise for a precious few well-defined metrics. It really should be at-a-glance level stuff 

Reports are where the detail is found. Most people actually want reports so they can mess  around with them in Excel, and attempts to resist this are futile so I have given up</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1307060926176039033 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1307060926176039033><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/114858490555531268/746e25b5e6bc3e73f5a5e166568b153b.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/230273923089039360/71063d00e7798c9b0b6e2ac39d6d0099.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title=.egk>EGK</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'1306958134849572884')"> I thought that it typically falls in one of those:

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1307093135247147059 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1307093135247147059><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/984386111709253672/23fac11e09942718016d6d4c58935a2e.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/230273923089039360/71063d00e7798c9b0b6e2ac39d6d0099.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title=.egk>EGK</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'1306955390784901240')"> Has it ever happened to you that you&#39;ve built data (dashboards, reports, etc.) for the organization and it ended up not really being used by anyone? </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=rebirch data-user-id=984386111709253672>reBirch</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Friday, November 15, 2024 6:21 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1307093135247147059>11/15/2024 6:21 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>We send a lot of regular scheduled reports to external and internal consumers, and a lot of times we find out they basically just ignore them. I once found that one report was nonfunctional for a month, and nobody bat an eye. 
Key reason is (IMO) product mismanagement and total lack of product vision.</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1307093644582588497 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1307093644582588497><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Friday, November 15, 2024 6:23 PM">6:23 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>The typical way this comes about: someone comes to a data analyst and asks to prepare an analysis/viz on an ad-hoc basis. The results turn out somehow helpful in that particular case, for a particular person. That person then gets the idea &quot;oh that&#39;s neat, can we now get this type of thing regularly?&quot; Team manager says &quot;sir yes sir&quot; and we implement it.</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1307093972484624526 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1307093972484624526><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Friday, November 15, 2024 6:24 PM">6:24 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Then after some time it turns out that the analysis only made sense in context of that specific discussion, or the person who originally requested now has a different focus, or maybe doesn&#39;t even work there any more.</span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Friday, November 15, 2024 6:25 PM">(edited)</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1307094474756722780 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1307094474756722780><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Friday, November 15, 2024 6:26 PM">6:26 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>IMO (but to be clear, I&#39;m talking with a &quot;technical product manager&quot; hat on but that&#39;s not my hat and I don&#39;t have that much experience, so I&#39;m happy to be corrected if someone is sure I&#39;m wrong) - the only way to really prevent this is very clear understanding of what your product is, and is <em>NOT</em> supposed to do.</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1307094672035811338 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1307094672035811338><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Friday, November 15, 2024 6:27 PM">6:27 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>And the willingness/political capital/recklessness/... to sometimes say no to implementing things that don&#39;t fit that vision.</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1311143278305083475 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1311143278305083475><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/440556927794282506/1e9166c623368655e98428031205d10a.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=trk12. data-user-id=440556927794282506>trk12</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Tuesday, November 26, 2024 10:35 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1311143278305083475>11/26/2024 10:35 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Hi guys, I am seeking help with a complex data modelling problem I am trying to solve. Was wondering if any kind soul with a good SQL expertise is able to help me. 

The question is: 
Obtain the average number of monthly active customers on the website over the past 6 months. An active customer is one that has purchased (event_name=&#39;Order Receipt) within the prior 12 months.

The table in use has the following structure: 
<em>customer_id (int)</em> : Unique id of the customer
<em>session_id(int)</em> Unique session id
<em>order_id(int)</em> Unique order id
<em>Event_id(PK - str)</em> Unique id for every click on the website
<em>Event_name(str)</em> Description of the event (can be ‘Product Page View’, ‘Add to Cart’, ‘View Basket’, ‘Order Receipt’) 
<em>event_date (TIMESTAMP)</em>  when the user performed the action (in UTC)</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1311144018243227738 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1311144018243227738><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/689583717064114274/d5e507d4a2ed8b2d968e140cc0f1ba1a.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/790363256086462474/a309a47de3b6e3d1e113b5035c3f7f34.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title=aarones>ImNuts43</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'1311142876016808016')"> how we feeling on dbt these days guys </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=wh00h00 data-user-id=689583717064114274>Wh00h00</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Tuesday, November 26, 2024 10:38 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1311144018243227738>11/26/2024 10:38 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Strange question. <div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1311144156235694101 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1311144156235694101><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/440556927794282506/1e9166c623368655e98428031205d10a.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/440556927794282506/1e9166c623368655e98428031205d10a.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title=trk12.>trk12</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'1311143278305083475')"> Hi guys, I am seeking help with a complex data modelling problem I am trying to solve. Was wondering if any kind soul with a good SQL expertise is able to help me. 

The question is: 
Obtain the average number of monthly active customers on the website over the past 6 months. An active customer is one that has purchased (event_name=&#39;Order Receipt) within the prior 12 months.

The table in use has the following structure: 
<em>customer_id (int)</em> : Unique id of the customer
<em>session_id(int)</em> Unique session id
<em>order_id(int)</em> Unique order id
<em>Event_id(PK - str)</em> Unique id for every click on the website
<em>Event_name(str)</em> Description of the event (can be ‘Product Page View’, ‘Add to Cart’, ‘View Basket’, ‘Order Receipt’) 
<em>event_date (TIMESTAMP)</em>  when the user performed the action (in UTC) </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=trk12. data-user-id=440556927794282506>trk12</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Tuesday, November 26, 2024 10:38 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1311144156235694101>11/26/2024 10:38 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>The best solution I could come up with so far is this. But I am not confident if its actually considering all the customers throughout a given month 

<code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">WITH monthly_active_customers AS (
    SELECT 
        FORMAT_TIMESTAMP(&#39;%Y-%m&#39;, TIMESTAMP(DATE_SUB(CURRENT_DATE(), INTERVAL month_offset MONTH))) AS month,
        COUNT(DISTINCT IFNULL(
            CAST(customer_id AS STRING), 
            CONCAT(&#39;GUEST_&#39;, CAST(session_id AS STRING))
        )) AS active_customers
    FROM 
        </code>online-retail-dbt.retail.tblEvent<code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">
    CROSS JOIN UNNEST(GENERATE_ARRAY(0, 5)) AS month_offset
    WHERE 
        Event_name = &#39;Order Receipt&#39;
        AND event_date BETWEEN 
            TIMESTAMP(DATE_SUB(DATE_SUB(CURRENT_DATE(), INTERVAL month_offset MONTH), INTERVAL 12 MONTH)) - INTERVAL 10 HOUR
            AND 
            TIMESTAMP(DATE_SUB(CURRENT_DATE(), INTERVAL month_offset MONTH)) - INTERVAL 10 HOUR
    GROUP BY 
        month
    ORDER BY 
        month
)
SELECT 
    ROUND(AVG(active_customers), 2) AS avg_monthly_active_customers
FROM 
    monthly_active_customers;</code></span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1311368199333347410 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1311368199333347410><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/3.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=philliphenry data-user-id=462278067474137088>PhillHenry</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Wednesday, November 27, 2024 1:29 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1311368199333347410>11/27/2024 1:29 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Example of one of our tests (healthcare sector). The prod code calculates the running total of the number of patients in a hospital on any given day given a dataframe not of patients but of events as that&#39;s what the system captures. 
<u>Synthetic data</u>
We create a dataframe of precisely <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">x</code> medical <em>events</em> over day range <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">R</code> for <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">y</code> different unique patients, distributed evenly over hospitals <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">{a,b,c}</code> where each patient is admitted on date <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">i mode R</code> and discharged <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">i mod w</code> days later (where <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">i</code> is the unique patient id in range <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">[0,y]</code>. The discharge date is null every <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">z</code> patients because we know we have bad data.

The data is random-ish but the same for any given set of parameters. It sounds complicated but it&#39;s one or two dozen lines that&#39;s used repeatedly across the test suite.
<u>Prod code</u>
The prod code needs to turn events into patient stays. What comes out of the sausage machine is the number of patients per hospital for each day in <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">R</code>.
<u>The assertions</u>
There are certain invariants we can assert on - eg the sum of occupancy deltas over the time frame is zero (ie, everybody who is admitted is ultimately discharged).</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1311368940139577344 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1311368940139577344><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Wednesday, November 27, 2024 1:31 PM">1:31 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>(Just re-read what I wrote. Fat-fingured the send so sent it prematurely - oops! - but apart from the <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">x</code>, <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">y</code>, <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">R</code>, <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">{a,b,c}</code> paragraph which is too detailed, this is what we&#39;re doing and we got really good results).</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1311377464336846899 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1311377464336846899><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/3.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=philliphenry data-user-id=462278067474137088>PhillHenry</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Wednesday, November 27, 2024 2:05 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1311377464336846899>11/27/2024 2:05 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>This tests some nice corner cases: if a patient is discharged the same day they&#39;re admitted, do they show up on that day&#39;s occupancy or not? If the discharge date is <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">null</code> what do we do with this patient? Obviously the algorithm must be robust and not count zombie patients who appear to be never discharged.</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1311506590117138523 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1311506590117138523><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/114858490555531268/746e25b5e6bc3e73f5a5e166568b153b.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/120645994923687937/a0b1bdb86d7551eb9267efe6cc7b5f40.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title=rexeh>Rexeh</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'1311277597468000337')"> Had an interesting debate about &quot;Unit tests&quot; in world of spark. I call testing a transformation function a unit test, because it&#39;s the smallest thing you can test and separatable. In the traditional sense of software dev I get it&#39;s not technically because it&#39;s dependent on pyspark/spark.

What do others think? Even got into debates about how it should &quot;all be mocked&quot; which they meant mocking spark which seems pure insanity </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=apatheticlamp data-user-id=114858490555531268>Lamp - Databricks #1 fan</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Wednesday, November 27, 2024 10:38 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1311506590117138523>11/27/2024 10:38 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>This is what I&#39;ve done for unit tests and it works well I think
Create a pyspark local fixture, mock input dataframe to a transformation function, mock output data that you expect from the transformation. Compare the two with testing pyspark built-ins.

Works pretty well, then if you&#39;re on databricks you can also use databricks connect and dry run the job from local with pyspark to ensure it works E2E</span></div></div></div></div></div>

Figure out what the pain points are, take notes on what&#39;s wrong, and see how well you can learn. Don&#39;t put a ton of pressure on yourself - most roles, and especially roles where there&#39;s a lot of spaghetti to inherit, don&#39;t expect you to hit the ground running too fast.</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1314739932736131153 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1314739932736131153><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/1296242089209626657/abea10f90dc6835f237e05650755d213.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author style=color:rgb(52,152,219) title=datacole data-user-id=1296242089209626657>Cole</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Friday, December 6, 2024 8:47 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1314739932736131153>12/6/2024 8:47 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Yeah so I mean I think the best way to enact change is to prove that change will be positive, so IMO:
<ul><li>When you get <em>new</em> work (new ETL pipeline to construct, or something similar), use the solution you would propose</li><li>Compare the simplicity and effort spent on that vs. how much time it would have taken with the current architecture</li><li>Repeat this process a couple more times so the proof of concept is clear, and be patient</li><li>Start making the case for a migration, estimate how much time you&#39;ll spend on the migration, do some napkin math regarding engineering hours spent on the migration vs engineering hours that will be saved by having better architecture, make any other supporting arguments (data quality, it sounds like)</li><li>Once you have approval, get migrating <img
